<div id="review_2441827361" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2441827361" />
    <a title="Kevin Kuhn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59568642-kevin-kuhn"><img alt="Kevin Kuhn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508679965p2/59568642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2441827361?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevin Kuhn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevin Kuhn" href="/user/show/59568642-kevin-kuhn">Kevin Kuhn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59568642-kevin-kuhn?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2441827361" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14626317544209980426">I’m a bit torn on this book. It was funny but not hilarious. I found the character’s to be a bit flat. I love Scalzi’s books, but if I have a complaint, it’s that all the character’s personalities seem too similar, even males and females. It was also short with the main story being about 280 pages. It has three Coda’s that take it to 314, and while they were interesting, they didn’t add a great deal to the story and they weren’t all that funny. So, I guess I went into this hoping for many belly </span>
  <span id="freeText14626317544209980426" style="display:none">I’m a bit torn on this book. It was funny but not hilarious. I found the character’s to be a bit flat. I love Scalzi’s books, but if I have a complaint, it’s that all the character’s personalities seem too similar, even males and females. It was also short with the main story being about 280 pages. It has three Coda’s that take it to 314, and while they were interesting, they didn’t add a great deal to the story and they weren’t all that funny. So, I guess I went into this hoping for many belly laughs, instead I found myself snickering often.<br /><br />On the other hand, I read it quickly, and I enjoyed it, and it was fun. Did I go in with too high of expectations? Probably. There is a quote on the back of the book, “I can honestly say I can’t think of another book that every made me laugh this much. Ever.” That might have been my problem. Does every novel have to groundbreaking or incredibly witty or mind blowing? Nope, the reality is that this is a fun, fast read. <br /><br />If you’re a sci-fi fan, the plot is what you might expect, just from reading the title. Ensign Andy Dahl has been assigned to the Universal Union (the double U – heh) Capital Ship Intrepid. He begins noticing a pattern that ‘redshirts’ assigned to away parties meet their demise on a much too regular basis. The rest of the novel follows Dahl and several other characters investigating this phenomenon and for their own self-preservation, trying to stop it. <br /><br />Scalzi got the idea for this story when he was working for Star Gate: Universe as a Creative Consultant. He approached it in an interesting way, I’m not sure he’s technically breaking the third wall in this story, maybe he created a fictional third wall, which is then broken. Anyway, I think most serious sci-fi fans will not be able to help being intrigued and entertained by this book.<br /><br />Three and a half stars, for this funny, fast read, with my rating possibly tainted by high expectations.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14626317544209980426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2087918107" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2087918107" />
    <a title="Brent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3742957-brent"><img alt="Brent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501210358p2/3742957.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2087918107?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brent" href="/user/show/3742957-brent">Brent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3742957-brent?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3742957-brent?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3742957-brent?shelf=on-hand">on-hand</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2087918107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2477900239831215064">Review 2.0 – Commissioned by me, several days after finishing the book and realizing that I had blubbered all over the original review (under the influence of the codas – I must admit.)<br/><br/>Consider it a pre-coda if you will.<br/><br/>What’s up with this book? Why are reviews all over the map on this one? <br/><br/>Because this story is like an ice-cream cone.<br/><br/>A triple scoop ice-cream cone, to be specific, one that presents a series of three distinct flavors that change as you work your way through it. <br/><br/>It begins as a pre</span>
  <span id="freeText2477900239831215064" style="display:none">Review 2.0 – Commissioned by me, several days after finishing the book and realizing that I had blubbered all over the original review (under the influence of the codas – I must admit.)<br /><br />Consider it a pre-coda if you will.<br /><br />What’s up with this book? Why are reviews all over the map on this one? <br /><br />Because this story is like an ice-cream cone.<br /><br />A triple scoop ice-cream cone, to be specific, one that presents a series of three distinct flavors that change as you work your way through it. <br /><br />It begins as a pretty funny, genre-aware, semi-parody of old school Star Trek. Because I grew up on the reruns of the original series, this flavor works really well for me.<br /><br />Slowly though, the flavor transitions into a more serious, meta-narrative quest reminiscent of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27003.The_Eyre_Affair__Thursday_Next___1_" title="The Eyre Affair (Thursday Next, #1) by Jasper Fforde" rel="nofollow noopener">The Eyre Affair</a> by Jasper Fforde. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Personally, my least favorite Star Trek episodes were always the “Let’s travel back to Earth and Interact with Ordinary People” ones. (Earth = boring, space = awesome.) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This flavor didn’t work so well for me and I kind of had to prod myself to wade through it at a couple of points. It gets better though and although the original tale ends on this flavor, the ending is still pretty satisfying and left me feeling, <i>“Hmm that was pretty good after all.”</i><br /><br />During the first coda flavors start to change again, and as we move out of the super-meta mind trip, I realize I have become emotionally invested in these characters. I tend to avoid sentimental stories and so maybe my threshold was low, but I found the last two codas to be very emotionally moving. (I might have cried, but I’ll deny it if you say anything.) It was in the glorious aftermath of these codas that I wrote my first review. <br /><br /> So I hope this straightens some things out<br /><br />--------- (Commence Review 1.0) ------------<br /><br />Thought number 1.)<br />It is difficult to write characters that you can laugh at and care about at the same time. Getting the comedic distance right is tricky, but Scalzi nails it here. <br /><br />Thought number 2)<br />The book is sort of billed as a Star Trek parody but its really not. <br /><br />Which is good. <br /><br />Because as fun as they might be, parodies really have no life of their own, like a parasite they rely on the original work for their vitality and relevance. But this story stands on its own, it takes turns being funny, intriguing, and at least to me, emotional moving. <br /><br />Thought number 3.)<br />I'm not sure what else I could ask for.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2477900239831215064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1139600128" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1139600128" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36819318-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485843897p2/36819318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1139600128?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/36819318-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36819318-scott?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1139600128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11704510423052879179">If there was a Booker for ‘Best Concept, Most Poorly Executed’, <i>Redshirts</i> would be hiring a tux and polishing an acceptance speech. This is a novel built on a great idea – imagine if all the disposable non-core-cast characters constantly killed for dramatic effect in sci-fi TV shows realised what was happening to them and rebelled against it, doing their damnedest to avoid going on missions with important, non-expendable crewmembers, trying to get transferred off the ship, etc.<br/><br/>From this great id</span>
  <span id="freeText11704510423052879179" style="display:none">If there was a Booker for ‘Best Concept, Most Poorly Executed’, <i>Redshirts</i> would be hiring a tux and polishing an acceptance speech. This is a novel built on a great idea – imagine if all the disposable non-core-cast characters constantly killed for dramatic effect in sci-fi TV shows realised what was happening to them and rebelled against it, doing their damnedest to avoid going on missions with important, non-expendable crewmembers, trying to get transferred off the ship, etc.<br /><br />From this great idea comes a thin, ailing novel desperate for a big bowl of Description (of which there is little) and an emergency transfusion of Interesting Characters (of which there are few). <br /><br />The lack of scene setting and description of the locations and objects in the story really got to me. I read the whole book with no real idea at all of what the central stage for the story – a large spaceship – looked like. The ship could have resembled a gigantic orange phallus wearing a Panama hat and I would have been none the wiser (actually that’s how I’m imagining it from now on- that would make a pretty great flagship). My guess is that Scalzi assumed his readers would be such big fans of the shows he is satirising that they would do all the work themselves, slotting in The Enterprise or Galactica as needed. The lack of descriptive text made every location in the story feeling like a series of shiny white rooms with no distinguishing features- spaceflight as designed by Steve Jobs. <br /><br />One of the reasons I love SF is the richness of the worlds and environments evoked in the genre – Alistair Reynolds’ gargantuan, baroque Lighthuggers, the beauty of Robert Mann’s planet Paradise, and the vivid memories I still carry from my time with Dan Simmon’s <i>Hyperion</i>. <i>Redshirts</i> in comparison is a blank slate, and while I don’t expect James Joyce level detail from SF novels I at least need a couple of descriptive hooks to hang my imagination on.<br /><br />Combined with a tendency for all the characters to sound the same <i>Redshirts</i> is a largely colourless novel. Still, it’s a fairly light story with some good funny bits and it flows OK, or at least it does until about two thirds in. At this point the story shifts location, along with tone, and gets way too meta for me, losing most of what had made it interesting.<br /><br />The last section of the story, a series of codas, also really jarred with me. What had been in large part a light comedic story is finished with some maudlin, sadly meaningful postscripts that seemed like a last-ditch attempt to make the story more worthy. <br /><br />Overall, this book was a bit of a bummer. From the blurb I was expecting great comedic SF – something along the lines of <i>Red Dwarf</i> or <i>The Hitchhikers Guide</i>. What I got was a novel that wasn’t consistently funny, or particularly well put together.<br /><br />I didn’t truly hate Redshirts, but it’s so much less than it could have been.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11704510423052879179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1249324715" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1249324715" />
    <a title="Darth J " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j"><img alt="Darth J " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456429148p2/18974711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1249324715?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darth J " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darth J " href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j">Darth J </a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5216694788404272380">If you're into stuff like this, <a href='http://manuelaantao.blogspot.com/2018/09/let-us-violate-cakes-together-redshirts.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>you can read the full review.</a><br/><br/><br/><br/>"Let us violate cakes together"<br/><br/><br/>In "Redshirts" by John Scalzi<br/><br/><br/><br/>(*day dreaming*)<br/><br/>I applied for a job to be a licensed fiction writer of sorts last year - it was working on flavour text and copy for the Star Trek Franchise. The interview was heavily focused on my ability to write within the constraints of their authorial voice and existing publications - as stringent as working for any publication with a house style. That's not quite, I admi</span>
  <span id="freeText5216694788404272380" style="display:none">If you're into stuff like this, <a href="http://manuelaantao.blogspot.com/2018/09/let-us-violate-cakes-together-redshirts.html" rel="nofollow noopener">you can read the full review.</a><br /><br /><br /><br />"Let us violate cakes together"<br /><br /><br />In "Redshirts" by John Scalzi<br /><br /><br /><br />(*day dreaming*)<br /><br />I applied for a job to be a licensed fiction writer of sorts last year - it was working on flavour text and copy for the Star Trek Franchise. The interview was heavily focused on my ability to write within the constraints of their authorial voice and existing publications - as stringent as working for any publication with a house style. That's not quite, I admit, the same thing as writing tie-in novels - but the attitude of IP holders to how licensed authors should write I experienced seems very much to be more like writing for a journal or newspaper than writing fiction - the job I applied for would very much have been technical or copy-writing about subjects that were fictional. Definitely a "specific skillset" as this Scalzi’s novel shows once again - but in retrospect I'm quite glad I didn't get the job.</span>

<div id="review_638924065" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/638924065" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/638924065?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/14896596-redshirts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer638924065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2386281086435786246">I started out thinking this would be a 4 star read. As it opens playing on the cliches of science fiction TV (specifically Star Trek) it is funny. In places it's hilarious.<br/><br/>I saw this book reviewed back when it first showed up and I read enough "blah" reviews that I decided I didn't want to put time or money into it. But recently I've had it recommended and seen some "rave reviews" about it so, I decided to give it a try. It's sort of an odd read as it almost travels in an descending arc. At firs</span>
  <span id="freeText2386281086435786246" style="display:none">I started out thinking this would be a 4 star read. As it opens playing on the cliches of science fiction TV (specifically Star Trek) it is funny. In places it's hilarious.<br /><br />I saw this book reviewed back when it first showed up and I read enough "blah" reviews that I decided I didn't want to put time or money into it. But recently I've had it recommended and seen some "rave reviews" about it so, I decided to give it a try. It's sort of an odd read as it almost travels in an descending arc. At first it's funny. You read the cliches you get the inside jokes and you laugh. So what happens?<br /><br />You get about a third of the way through the book and the book's outlook, direction and premise change. It takes on a semi-serious tone and then goes for almost a completely serious tone with a "weirdness" factor. To say much more than that is to give spoilers but I will say that by the time you get to the "Codas" it's pretty much moved from a funny tongue in cheek science fiction "take-off" to a sad yawner.<br /><br />I've read books by Scalzi that are great so I had hope for this and after the "great reviews" I was looking forward to it. <br /><br />I think now I may return it to Audible. Sorry...sorry I can't truly recommend it, sorry I didn't enjoy it more, sorry that in honesty I have to say that while I didn't hate it I don't really like it.<br /><br />Too bad as it's a good idea and had it not started trying to take itself seriously it could have been many times better than it is. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2386281086435786246" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_408653930" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/408653930" />
    <a title="Char " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6581119-char"><img alt="Char " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415394568p2/6581119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/408653930?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Char " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Char " href="/user/show/6581119-char">Char </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/22896671-redshirts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6581119-char?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6581119-char?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6581119-char?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer408653930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8253381770938409831">As a big fan of Star Trek in almost all of its incarnations, I thought for sure I would adore this audio book, especially since it was narrated by Wil Wheaton. I was partially right. <br/><br/>I <i> did </i> adore Wil Wheaton's narration. The only problem I had with it were the "he saids" and "she saids". There was one of these tags after (nearly) every single sentence of dialogue. Enough already! I guess this really isn't Wheaton's fault, but maybe he could have de-emphasized the tags a bit?<br/><br/>The story itself was</span>
  <span id="freeText8253381770938409831" style="display:none">As a big fan of Star Trek in almost all of its incarnations, I thought for sure I would adore this audio book, especially since it was narrated by Wil Wheaton. I was partially right. <br /><br />I <i> did </i> adore Wil Wheaton's narration. The only problem I had with it were the "he saids" and "she saids". There was one of these tags after (nearly) every single sentence of dialogue. Enough already! I guess this really isn't Wheaton's fault, but maybe he could have de-emphasized the tags a bit?<br /><br />The story itself was a bit of a letdown. Yes, it was funny, (laugh out loud funny at some points), but the story didn't hold together for me. I found it to be a wee bit silly. Oddly though, I loved the 3 codas at the end. Enough so that I will definitely be seeking out John Scalzi's other works. <br /><br />Overall, this was a funny story that didn't make much sense, but I'm okay with that. If you're a Star Trek fan and you like Will Wheaton, you might be okay with it too. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8253381770938409831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3626741672" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3626741672" />
    <a title="Ian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31384949-ian"><img alt="Ian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584889764p2/31384949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3626741672?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian" href="/user/show/31384949-ian">Ian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/14896596-redshirts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31384949-ian?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31384949-ian?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31384949-ian?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31384949-ian?shelf=4-star-sci-fi">4-star-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31384949-ian?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3626741672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6656032999322776835">My understanding of what this book was about changed as the story progressed. I take my hat off to the author for the skilful way he did this, and for the way he gets the story to work on different levels. Unfortunately, my enjoyment was a bit reduced by the 3 “codas” at the end of the main novel, which I found a bit saccharine for my taste.<br/><br/>The first quarter of the novel is a very funny send up of “Star Trek”, featuring the adventures of the crew of the Universal Union Ship “Intrepid”. I listene</span>
  <span id="freeText6656032999322776835" style="display:none">My understanding of what this book was about changed as the story progressed. I take my hat off to the author for the skilful way he did this, and for the way he gets the story to work on different levels. Unfortunately, my enjoyment was a bit reduced by the 3 “codas” at the end of the main novel, which I found a bit saccharine for my taste.<br /><br />The first quarter of the novel is a very funny send up of “Star Trek”, featuring the adventures of the crew of the Universal Union Ship “Intrepid”. I listened to the audiobook narrated by Wil Wheaton. Possibly it was his delivery of the lines, but it’s been years since I laughed this much at a book. Funniest of all was the chapter that featured the crew on shore leave, and Ensign Dahl’s conversation with the drunken Lt. Kerensky. Although I personally found the book funny, I’ll just say that there are many books/films/comedians that others find hilarious that don’t do anything for me. We all have our own sense of humour.<br /><br />The laughs get fewer after the first quarter or so, but the story does have to move on, as the junior members of the Intrepid’s crew realise their prospects are about as good as those of a WW2 kamikaze pilot, and decide to do something about that.<br /><br />The 3 “codas” add another level to the complexity of the storyline. Each is a sort of epilogue focused on a particular character. At one point in coda 3, the lead character is accused of talking “like a character in a lifetime movie who’s just been told she has breast cancer.” I had very similar thoughts, and actually I felt all 3 of the codas were written in that style. Ultimately, this becomes one of those novels that’s about the choices we make, and how things might have turned out differently. At the end of the main novel my rating was at a solid four stars. I considered knocking off a star after reading the 3 codas, but decided in the end to err on the generous side. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6656032999322776835" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1840804660" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1840804660" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1840804660?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/14896596-redshirts">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1840804660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4354053927013190826"><i>"Because I need to know. I always needed to know."</i><br/><br/>This is probably how most Trekkies have felt over the years. <br/><br/>For those here, who don't know, here's a little background information:<br/>In the original <b>Star Trek</b> series (the one with Shatner as Kirk and Nimoy as Spok), there were usually one or two people in red shirts that are sent to some unexplored panet together with two or three main characters. These lowly-ranking people had never been seen before - and never again afterwards either. Because th</span>
  <span id="freeText4354053927013190826" style="display:none"><i>"Because I need to know. I always needed to know."</i><br><br>This is probably how most Trekkies have felt over the years. <br><br>For those here, who don't know, here's a little background information:<br>In the original <b>Star Trek</b> series (the one with Shatner as Kirk and Nimoy as Spok), there were usually one or two people in red shirts that are sent to some unexplored panet together with two or three main characters. These lowly-ranking people had never been seen before - and never again afterwards either. Because they die. Always. Out of 59 killed crew members in the course of the first season, 43 were such Redshirts. It became an instant classic joke, people keep making fun of it to this day (just google Redshirt meme and you'll see).<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504978067i/23856157._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>On top of that, certain plot points just never made any sense. Some effects didn't either (like people getting thrown around the bridge of the starship when they had to do some serious maneuvering).<br><br>So in this book, the author addresses all of that by incorporating it in a humorous way and then letting the characters become aware of some senseless plot points and weird ways of dying even.<br><br>Make no mistake, this book was written for geeks and nerds. Thus, there are a lot of easter eggs in here - at several points in the book I nodded, remembering exactly which episode the author must have been talking about - on top of the fact that the audiobook narrator is no other than "Wesley Crusher". <br><br>However, as amusing especially the beginning of the book was, it kind of suffered from much the same problem the actual series did too. There was a lot thrust in (on purpose, but still), convoluting the story, and at some point it just wasn't all that funny any more (until the end). Since this was most probably done on purpose because that is exactly what always happened on the show, I'll make allowances for it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504978067i/23856158.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After that, we have 3 codas that were less amusing and more tackling some bigger issues. <br>The first is about writers block. An interesting message addressed here was that it doesnt matter THAT someone dies, because we all do - HOW one dies matters, however. That is true in real life as well, though - naturally - nobody wants to die if it can be helped.<br>The second one is about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Matthew, the son of one of the writers, who was brain-dead after a motorcycle accident and was "brought back" by the Redshirts <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, thus talking about some existential questions. This got to me in in a number of ways. <br>The third one is about Samantha, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[who receives a box of videos and pictures of "herself" and "her husband" before "she" died <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, talking about the big what-if in life (what other lives could have been). The horrible dating episodes were kinda fun in a tragic way. *lol* And I'm glad to have a character like Brian addressing <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that he believes in The One True Love, a soul-mate, even though he acknowledges that it's not like that for everyone <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> because that is exactly how I think and feel about it and other people getting it is rare.<br><br>And all three tie into the story of the Redshirts, of course, making it all a bit meta. The codas and their more sincere tone prove that Scalzi didn't just mean to amuse and entertain, but also to get readers thinking. Not bad. Not bad at all.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4354053927013190826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1449837645" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1449837645" />
    <a title="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks"><img alt="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592760668p2/13716524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1449837645?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" href="/user/show/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks">Evelina | AvalinahsBooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">any sci-fi fan</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Evelina | AvalinahsBooks by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/22832688-efka">Efka</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks?shelf=books-of-2017">books-of-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks?shelf=fun-or-funny">fun-or-funny</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1449837645" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13882696594417906193">★★★★☆ 4 stars I'm sure most of you have heard of <i><b>Redshirts.</b> </i>And let's admit, Scalzi is a pretty well-known writer, having received many awards (the 2013 Hugo Award for Best Novel for this one being among them), as well as having worked as a consultant to the TV series Stargate Universe, if any of you are familiar with that show.<br/><br/>(I have been known as a fierce fan of Stargate SG-1, although I didn't like Stargate Universe that much.)<br/><br/>And yet, despite all the fame (I nearly wrote <i>famousity, </i>what??),</span>
  <span id="freeText13882696594417906193" style="display:none">★★★★☆ 4 stars I'm sure most of you have heard of <i><b>Redshirts.</b> </i>And let's admit, Scalzi is a pretty well-known writer, having received many awards (the 2013 Hugo Award for Best Novel for this one being among them), as well as having worked as a consultant to the TV series Stargate Universe, if any of you are familiar with that show.<br><br>(I have been known as a fierce fan of Stargate SG-1, although I didn't like Stargate Universe that much.)<br><br>And yet, despite all the fame (I nearly wrote <i>famousity, </i>what??), this is the first book of Scalzi's that I have read. And you know what?<br><i>
  <b>It was goooooooood.</b>
</i><br>You can read the full review <a href="https://goo.gl/5Jh4HS" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">on my blog</a> (complete with images and book buy links).<br><br>So what is this book about? Let me write up a quick synopsis for you:<br><br>Ensign Andrew Dahl has just been assigned to a prestigious post on the flagship Intrepid, a spaceship of the Universal Union since 2456, and he is thrilled, until he realizes that:<br><br>1. The captain orders away missions quite often, and the crew do their best to... well, avoid even being seen;<br>2. That might be because <i>EVERY</i> away mission involves some kind of lethal confrontation with alien forces;<br>3. The ship’s captain, its chief science officer, and the handsome Lieutenant Kerensky always survive these confrontations;<br>4. And, at least one low-ranked crew member is, sadly, always killed.<br>As trying to find out what's going on is almost equatable to staying alive, Andrew sets out to do just that, and what he finds out about the ship is as crazy and unbelievable as it is true.<br><br>If you're still unclear about what a redshirt stands for and what their approximate chances of survival are, I present to you this handy image:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425401518i/13884492._SX540_.jpg" width="392" height="283" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I totally found this image online. Sorry for not crediting through lack of knowing who to credit.<br><br>So, let me start the review. We can sum up my reading experience to this:<br><br><i>
  <b>Phase 1.<br>"THIS BOOK!" + constant laughter</b>
</i><br>This phase was naturally the most enjoyable. There was definitely more than one time that I laughed out loud, whether home alone or with people around. At one point, I kept looking up, going <i>"THIS BOOK!" </i>to my boyfriend and then laughing out loud. As of that point, Redshirts has simply been known as <i>
  <b>THIS BOOK. </b>
</i>My boyfriend still knows what I'm referring to when I say that.<br><i>
  <b>Phase 2.<br>What? No! Don't make it lame!</b>
</i><br>Suffice to say without spoiling too much, is that the theories the low-rank crew develops about what's going on on their ship are... Slightly crazy. Slightly... Damaging to the 4th wall. More like, tearing it down. Or completely demolishing it. Something like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490612175ra/22326715.gif" width="339" height="260" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Said part of the story has many references to the Star Trek Enterprise. I didn't like them being voiced that much. I'm... Not sure I liked the 4th wall being broken at all. At least in <i>
  <b>THIS WAY.</b>
</i><br>But don't get me wrong. The book is still unbelievably funny at this point.<br><br><i>
  <b>Phase 3.<br>NO, PLEASE, just not this serious stuff... Not in this</b>
</i><b> book!</b><br>This part can be otherwise referred to as The Codas. It's about 70-80% into the book, so it's pretty much the epilogue. To be honest, this is where the actual story ends and we get to tie up loose ends through the POVs of secondary (I'd say even tertiary) characters. We don't follow the main characters anymore.<br><i>
  <b>So yes. I guess from Phase 2 and Phase 3 being like this, you'd probably think I didn't like the book.</b>
</i><br><i>
  <b>You'd be wrong though!</b>
</i><br><br>Funny enough, but the first part and the humor still completely makes up for the breach of the 4th wall, as well as The Codas. To be fair, most fans <i>DO</i> think The Codas were too dampening and philosophical to belong in this book. But you can choose not to read them, I guess (they don't add much to the story anyway). Apart from that though, it was an <i>
  <b>extremely enjoyable read, especially if you're looking for something to make you laugh.</b>
</i><br><br>To sum it up, Redshirts is <i>
  <b>a sci-fi novel bordering on parody that will make you laugh out loud</b>
</i>. If you dislike scientific terms in sci-fi, you're more likely to find them made fun of in this one. If you've ever seen a single episode of Star Trek or at least know the general fan culture, you'll find that this book will bite at the ideas that make up that show and shows like that in general. This is a great vacation from hard sci-fi and simply from tough or serious books. Do give it a go, even if you don't normally read a lot of sci-fi stories!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13882696594417906193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1910408936" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1910408936" />
    <a title="HBalikov" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/929238-hbalikov"><img alt="HBalikov" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271764879p2/929238.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1910408936?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="HBalikov" class="user" itemprop="url" name="HBalikov" href="/user/show/929238-hbalikov">HBalikov</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17225428-redshirts">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1910408936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6840698702953180131">Scalzi is a top science fiction writer but occasionally, see my review of Agent to the Stars, he takes a more humorous view of the genre. This book falls into that category.<br/><br/>To properly appreciate this yarn, you should have at least a passing acquaintance with the original TV series, Star Trek. The Second Generation and its successors (including the series of movies) are not as directly in his sights. The redshirts referred to in the title are those minor members of the ship’s crew that are inclu</span>
  <span id="freeText6840698702953180131" style="display:none">Scalzi is a top science fiction writer but occasionally, see my review of Agent to the Stars, he takes a more humorous view of the genre. This book falls into that category.<br /><br />To properly appreciate this yarn, you should have at least a passing acquaintance with the original TV series, Star Trek. The Second Generation and its successors (including the series of movies) are not as directly in his sights. The redshirts referred to in the title are those minor members of the ship’s crew that are included in the “away team,” the group of sturdy spacers who beam down to a planet or over to an alien ship to investigate some threat. Somehow, by attack, plague, enchantment, etc., they are eliminated while the well-known members of the crew survive and the series continues.<br /><br />Starting with this premise, Scalzi creates a plot where the newer members of the crew become aware of this “casualty rate” and start to figure out ways to avoid being part of the away team. Scalzi is very imaginative in terms of his permutations and appropriately “cheesy” when it comes to some of the monsters and plot turns. <br /><br />Since my “Star Trek” friends and I have often used this observation as a gag for difficult situations that we would rather not be part of, I found the plot quite appealing. If you don’t, you have been warned.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6840698702953180131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bV4wigctv6/XV6T/Np279BzfMQw1DmOfmMPvVRzurG9eqp+MtL9SCCIQ0ugGEnmNJRh98xCZnn7FO5QCqa0RkA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UHcNgna+mQEbzeHIaTKZ2OU9zjXBAj2lhCeVu3rZi4Vjg6KExSx0pu6Kl99ZvVuh3PqCyuSVwETZ3+7sz5o2eg==')})
  }
//]]>
